## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where the restoring force is a nonlinear function of position x, possibly with nonlinear damping (function of v) and/or external periodic driving (function of t). Classical nonlinear oscillator models like Duffing, Van der Pol, and pendulum equations are the primary candidates.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple restoring force)
- Duffing oscillator (unforced, undamped): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Duffing oscillator (damped, driven): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing equation)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * v * (1 + c1 * x**2) + c2 * x (nonlinear damping with position-dependent coefficient)
- Pendulum approximation: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (gravitational pendulum restoring torque)
- Damped nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (Duffing with linear damping)
- Quintic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order nonlinear restoring force)
- Softening spring with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * v (asymmetric restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * x**2 + c2 * v (position-dependent damping)
- Cubic damping oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v**3 (nonlinear velocity-dependent friction)
- Driven pendulum: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (damped driven pendulum)
- Helmholtz oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (quadratic nonlinearity in restoring force)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity nonlinearity)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) + c2 * x (time-modulated stiffness)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) → symmetric potential wells preserving oscillation symmetry
- Even-power position terms (x²) → asymmetric potential indicating broken symmetry in restoring force
- Products v*x² or v*(1-x²) → amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of self-excited oscillators (Van der Pol type)
- Sinusoidal functions of position sin(c*x) → periodic potential / pendulum-like geometry with bounded restoring force
- Cosine or sine of time cos(c*t) → external periodic driving force causing forced oscillation or resonance
- Cubic position term x³ with opposite sign to linear term → Duffing-type hardening or softening spring nonlinearity
- Velocity terms proportional to v → energy dissipation (negative coefficient) or energy injection (positive coefficient)
- Mixed terms like x*v → phase-space-dependent forces indicating non-conservative or gyroscopic coupling
- Parametric terms x*cos(c*t) → parametric excitation leading to Mathieu-type instabilities
